Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly. and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation where text detection optical character recognition language translation and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents. avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tited. partly shadowed or closer at the top than at the botom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole trame and again over the upper portion. because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A ftrame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still, or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count recognition confidence. focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character emor rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should te able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototyre described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom. Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur. The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses Work Bench A weartble translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection, and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right. hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason, several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction. edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation. and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted. partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom. Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur. The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement, mild gamima correction. edge-preserving fitering. and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence. focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility A maintenance team operates a hybrid-energy station on a dry plateau several hours from the nearest town The station supplies a medical room. a radio repeater. weather instruments. refrigeration. and emergency lighting Solar panels provide most of the daily energy. lithium batteries cover the evening demand, and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms Because winter roads can remain closed for days, the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current, temperature, fan speed, and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available, and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025, solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration The controller did not shut down'the entire station It disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting. started the backup generator. and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults: debris covering part of the solar array, wear in a fan bearing, and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector These possibilities were ranked. but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened. a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece Equipment labels contained model numbers, safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages The local translation system first checked whether the Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility reserved for long storms. Because winter roads can remain closed for days. the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current, temperature, fan speed, and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds. Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available, and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025, solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration The controller did not shut down the entire station It disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting. started the backup generator, and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults debris covering part of the solar array, wear in a fan bearing. and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector These possibilities were ranked but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened, a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece Equipment labels contained model numbers, safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible It rejected frames with a missing edge. heavy glare, severe perspective distortion. or poor sharpness in the upper region Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward If the label was off centre, a simple left or right instruction was played These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service vehicle Text boxes were arranged in reading order and grouped into paragraphs The offline translation model passed one region at a time to the speech engine, and a brief tone marked every transition

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most usefu when t behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly. and hear a dlear rendering without holding a telephore or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a copact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech syrthesis are performed. The cormplete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive Image acquisition is the first major difficuty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tited, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it it locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks thal a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain sof. A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree. Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or nght, hold sil or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition. Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters. while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction. edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence. focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instea

The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly. and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation. where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camers view. Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation. where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents. avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly. and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. in the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language transtation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition. Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters. while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason, several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calcula

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection, and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted. partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom. Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still, or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

Autonomous Monitoring of a Remote Hybrid-Energy Station An isolated plateau station powers a medical clinic, radio repeater, solar panels, lithium batteries, and a compact diesel generator Because communications loads always receive priority On 18 October 2025, a dust storm reduced solar generation by 34 percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature increased by 8 C, and the inverter fan developed an unusual low-frequency vibration Rather than shut down the station the controller disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting, and started the backup generator Diagnostic software separated the incident into three likely faults debris on the solar array, wear in a fan bearing, and rising contact resistance at a battery connector. After the storm, a head-mounted camera read equipment labels and alarm codes, which a local processor compared with an offline manual Sensitive images were not uploaded to the cloud. The capture program required the complete label to remain inside a safe border and checked sharpness across the full frame and its upper region Spoken guidance requested a step backward when an edge was missing, and four stable observations were required Engineers later confirmed the suggested order clear the panels, replace the bearing, then tighten the connector The six-minute repair caused no critical interruption Trustworthy automation must expose uncertainty and leave final responsibility with the human operator

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur. The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters. while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation. where text detection, optical character recognition. language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted. partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion. because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility A maintenance team operates a hybnd-energy station on a dry plateau several hours from the nearest town. The station supplies a medical room. a radio repeater, weather instruments. refrigeration. and emergency lighting Solar panels provide most of the daily energy, lithium batteries cover the evening demand, and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms. Because winter roads can remain closed for days, the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current, temperature, fan speed, and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available and medical and communications loads always receive pnonty Dunng a dust storm on 18 October 2025. solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration The controller did not shut down the entire station It disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting started the backup generator. and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults. debris covering part of the solar array. wear in a fan bearing. and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector These possibilities were ranked but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened, a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece Equipment labels contained model numbers, safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible It rejected frames with a missing edge heavy glare severe perspective distortion. or poor sharpness in the upper region Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward If the label was off centre, a simple left or right instruction was played These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service vehicle Text boxes were arranged in reading order and grouped into paragraphs The offine translation model passed one region at a time to the speech engine, and a brief tone marked every transition

Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility A maintenance team operates a hybrid-energy station on a dry plateau several hours from the nearest town. The station supplies a medical room. a radio repeater. weather instruments refrigeration and emergency lighting Solar panels provide most of the daily energy. lithium batteries cover the evening demand and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms Because winter roads can remain closed for days, the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current. temperature fan speed, and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025 solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration. The controller did not shut down the entire station It disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting. started the backup generator, and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults debris covering part of the solar array, wear in a fan bearing. and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector These possibilities were ranked. but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened. a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece. Equipment labels contained model numbers. safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible It rejected frames with a missing edge heavy glare severe perspective distortion or poor sharpness in the upper region Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward If the label was off centre. a simple left or right instruction was played. EXTRACTED TEXT:
A maintenance team operates a hybrid-energy station on a dry plateau several hours from the nearest town. The station supplies a medical room a radio repeater, weather instruments, refrigeration, and emergency lighting. Solar panels provide most of the daily energy, lithium batteries cover the evening demand, and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms Because winter roads can remain closed for days. the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current, temperature fan speed. and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available, and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025, solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes. Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration. The controller did not shut down the entire station. It disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting. started the backup generator. and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults: debris covering part of the solar array. wear in a fan bearing, and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector These possibilities were ranked. but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened. a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece. Equipment labels contained model numbers, safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages. The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible. It rejected frames with a missing edge. heavy glare. severe perspective distortion, or poor sharpness in the upper region Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward if the label was off centre, a simple left or right instruction was played These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service vehicle Text boxes were arranged in reading order and grouped inte paragraphs The offline translation model passed one region at a time to the speech engine and a brief tone marked every transition

CODE VERSION: pipeline_cli_box4b.py
RUN NUMBER  : 1
IMAGE FILE  : capture_cli_001_20260722_143716.jpg
TEXT REGIONS: 6
PAGE TITLES : 1
HEADINGS    : 1
PARAGRAPHS  : 4
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count recognition confidence, focus statistics. and processing time confidence alone
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses Awearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an e  a labay demoaon The ur hlbe ale to face a prited page pause brely, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right. hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement. mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time. Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still, or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thiresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast eor

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses 日 Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted. partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right. hold still or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. severai preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement mild gamma correction. edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive tinarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence. focus statistics, and processing time Ground-tuth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses 日 Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted. partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right. hold still or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs. The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement mild gamma correction. edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive tinarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count. recognition confidence. focus statistics, and processing time Ground-tuth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted, partly shadowed. or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the imagé, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right. hold still, or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time confidence alone

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration. The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly, and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer. Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation. where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation. and speech synthesis are performed. The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents. avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only sharpening can create bright halos around letters. while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement. mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right. hold still or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering. and adaptive binarization. Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly. and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation. and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service. This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty. A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view. The page may be tilted. partly shadowed. or closer at the top than at the bottom. Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it. It locates groups of text. estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image. and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft. A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on aonfidence alone

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page, pause briefly. and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation, where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted, partly shadowed, or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion, because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right, hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters, while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes For that reason several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale, local contrast enhancement. mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on confidence alone

Field Evaluation of Wearable Translation Glasses A wearable translation system is most useful when it behaves like an ordinary tool rather than a laboratory demonstration The user should be able to face a printed page. pause briefly. and hear a clear rendering without holding a telephone or searching through menus. In the prototype described here, a small camera is mounted near eye level and connected to a compact computer Video is sent over a local link to a processing workstation. where text detection, optical character recognition, language translation, and speech synthesis are performed The complete pipeline operates without a cloud service This arrangement protects sensitive documents, avoids delays caused by an unstable internet connection. and allows every software component to be measured independently Image acquisition is the first major difficulty A person wearing glasses cannot easily see whether all four edges of a page are inside the camera view The page may be tilted. partly shadowed or closer at the top than at the bottom Motion from breathing and head movement also creates blur The capture controller therefore examines every incoming frame before saving it It locates groups of text, estimates whether the document occupies a useful fraction of the image, and checks that a safe border remains around the detected region. Sharpness is measured over the whole frame and again over the upper portion because a slanted sheet often appears clear near the bottom while the first lines remain soft A frame is accepted only after several consecutive observations agree. Spoken prompts tell the wearer to step back, move left or right. hold still. or improve the lighting After capture, the image is converted to grayscale and corrected only when the correction improves measured recognition Excessive sharpening can create bright halos around letters. while aggressive thresholding can erase punctuation and thin strokes. For that reason. several preprocessing alternatives are tested on the same stored photographs The comparison includes raw grayscale. local contrast enhancement, mild gamma correction, edge-preserving filtering, and adaptive binarization Each alternative is evaluated using character count, recognition confidence, focus statistics, and processing time Ground-truth text is retained for important experiments so that character error rate and word error rate can be calculated instead of relying on
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

EXTRACTED TEXT:
Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility A maintenance team operates a hybrid-energy station on a dry plateau several hours from the nearest town. The station supplies a medical room, a radio repeater, weather instruments, refrigeration. and emergency lighting Solar panels provide most of the daily energy. lithium batteries cover the evening demand, and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms Because winter roads can remain closed for days, the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage. current, temperature, fan speed, and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available, and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025, solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes. Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration The controller did not shut down the entire station. It disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting. started the backup generator, and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults: debris covering part of the solar array, wear in a fan bearing. and increasing contact resistance at a battery connector These possibilities were ranked. but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened. a technician approached the cabinet while wearing a head-mounted camera and an earpiece Equipment labels contained model numbers, safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages. The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible It rejected frames with a missing edge heavy glare. severe perspective distortion. or poor sharpness in the upper region. Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored. If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward If the label was off centre, a simple left or right instruction was played These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication P InteretPC Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service vehicle Text boxes were arranged in reading order and grouped into paragraphs The offline translation model passed one region at a time to the speech engine, and a brief tone marked every transition

Offline Inspection at a Remote Energy Facility A maintenance team operates a hybrid-energy station on a dry plateau several hours from the nearest town The station supplies a medical room a radio repester. weather instruments. refrigeration. and emergency lighting Solar panels provide most of the daily energy. lithium batteries cover the evening demand. and a compact diesel generator is reserved for long storms. Because winter roads can remain closed for days the control cabinet stores detailed measurements locally Voltage current. temperature. fan speed. and vibration are sampled every two hundred milliseconds Only compressed summaries are transmitted when the radio link becomes available. and medical and communications loads always receive priority During a dust storm on 18 October 2025. solar output fell by thirty-four percent in fifteen minutes Battery-cabinet temperature rose by eight degrees Celsius. and the inverter fan developed an unusual low- frequency vibration The controller did not shut down the entire station. It disconnected secondary heaters, reduced selected lighting. started the backup generator. and issued a maintenance warning Diagnostic software identified three plausible faults debris covering part of the solar array. wear in a fan bearing. and increasing contact resistance at a battery cosnector These possibilities were ranked. but none was presented as certain because the measurements could be explained by more than one physical condition When the storm weakened, a technician approached the cabinet while wearng a head-mounted camera and an earpiece. Equipment labels contained model numbers, safety notices, alarm codes, and short repair instructions in several languages The local translation system first checked whether the complete label was visible It rejected frames with a missing edge. heavy glare. severe perspective distortion, or poor sharpness in the upper region Four stable frames were required before a photograph was stored. If the target was too close, the earpiece asked the technician to step backward If the label was off centre, a simple left or nght instruction was played. These cues were deliberately brief so they would not compete with environmental sounds or safety communication Accepted images were processed on a workstation inside the service vehicle Text boxes were arranged in reading order and grouped into paragraphs. The offline translation model passed one region at a time to the speech engine, and a brief tone marked every transition

EXTRACTED TEXT:
偏远地区混合能源站的自主监测与维护 一座高原试验站依靠太阳能阵列、锂电池和小型柴油发电机供电。微电 网需要特续支持诊所、无线电中继、气象设备和安全照明。冬季道路可能 封闭数日，网络也不稳定因此本地控制器每二百毫秒采集电压、电流、 温度与振动数据，并在能源不足时优先保障医疗和通信负载。完整记录保 存在站内，只有压缩后的状态摘要会在链路恢复时发送到控制中心。 二〇二五年十月十八日一场沙尘风暴使太阳能输出在十五分钟内下降 百分之三十四电池柜温度升高八摄氏度，逆变器风扇还出现异常低频摄 动。控制器没有关闭整座电站，而是断开非必要加热装置、降低部分照明 功率并启动各用发电机。诊断模块随后提出三个可能原因太阳能板被碎 局遮挡、风扇轴承磨损，以及电池连接器的接触电阻上升。 风暴减弱后，技术员用头戴式摄像设备读取铭牌、序列号和报警代码 本地处理单元再与离线维护手册进行比对。由干资料涉及关键基础设施 图像没有上传云端。采集程序先确认整个标签位于安全边界内并分别检 查全图和上部区域的清晰度：若画面被裁切，耳机会提示向左、向右或向 后移动。目标只有连续四帧稳定且文字足够清楚时才会保存。第二天的日 志表明，自动排序与人工判断一致：先清理面板，再更换风扇轴承，最后 紧固电池端子。处置用了六分钟，关键服务未中断。这说明可靠的自动化 必须解释判断、承认不确定性，并把最终决定留给人。
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
TRANSLATED TEXT:
Autonomous monitoring and maintenance of hybrid power stations in remote areas A plateau test station relies on solar arrays, lithium batteries and a small diesel generator to power it. Microelectronics networks are needed to support clinics, radio relay, weather equipment and safety lighting. Roads may be closed for days in winter, and the network is unstable, so local controllers collect voltage, current, temperature and vibration data every 200 milliseconds, and prioritize medical and communications loads when energy is scarce. Complete logs are stored on the station, and only compressed status summaries are sent to the control center when the link is restored. On October 18, 2005, a dust storm caused solar output to drop in fifteen minutes. The temperature of the battery cabinet rose by 34 percent to eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter fan also showed abnormally low frequency vibrations. Instead of shutting down the entire power plant, the controller disconnects unnecessary heating devices, lowers partial lighting, power and starts the various generators. Diagnostic modules then suggested three possible causes of the solar panel breaking: the block shading, fan bearing wear, and the rise in contact resistance of the battery connector. After the storm weakened, technicians used head-mounted cameras to read the markings, serial numbers and alarm codes of the local processing unit and compare them with the offline maintenance manual. The images are not uploaded to the cloud because of the information involved in critical infrastructure. The capture process first confirms that the entire label is within the safety boundary and checks separately the clarity of the whole image and the upper area: if the image is cropped, the earpiece is prompted to move left, right or backwards. The target is saved only when the sequence of four lines is stable and the text is clear enough. The next day's logs showed that the automatic sorting was consistent with the artificial judgment: first the panel was cleaned, then the fan bearings were replaced, and finally the battery terminals were tightened. The disposal took six minutes and critical services were not interrupted. This shows that reliable automation must interpret judgments, acknowledge uncertainty, and leave the final decision to humans.

TRANSLATED TEXT:
10 Self-monitoring and maintenance of hybrid power stations in the two countries A high-power test price is a really big solar array, grade battery and small rack and motor, electricity, electricity. The network needs to have three support rooms, radio in the middle, weather conditions and full lighting, winter passage may be closed for days and the same connection is not determined, so the local controller collects phone calls every two hundred table seconds, current temperature and reassurance data and in case of insufficient energy priority to ensure medical and health care services, complete school security is present in the station, only from the later state to be sent to the control center in time to make a reply to the control center. On October 18, 2015, a sandstorm caused the solar energy output to decrease by fifteen minutes. The temperature of the battery cabinet rose by 34% to eight degrees Celsius. The controller does not shut down the entire power station, but disconnects unnecessary heating devices, green low-light parts of the power and stops the various generators. The breakage of the modules was followed by three possible causes: solar panels were broken and the insulation was blocked. The fan bearing wear, as well as the contact resistance of the battery connector rise. After the storm weakened, technicians used head-mounted imaging equipment to test the postcards, serial numbers and emergency code of the local processing unit and then compared it with the offline maintenance manual, since the information involved a blank image of the base you did not upload to the cloud. The retriever first confirms that the entire label is within the safety zone and checks the clarity of the whole picture and the upper area separately: if the face is counted, the earpiece is prompted to move left, right or backwards. The target is only saved when the quadrant is stable and the text is clear enough, and the log of the next day shows that the automatic sorting is consistent with artificial judgement, first cleaning the panel, then replacing the fan and finally tightening the battery terminals. The disposal took six minutes and critical services were not interrupted. This shows that reliable automation must be interpreted judgementally. In the meantime, I'm not going to go into detail about what happened, but I'm going to go into detail about what happened, and I'm going to talk about what happened.

TRANSLATED TEXT:
Autonomous monitoring and maintenance of hybrid power stations in remote areas A plateau test station relies on solar arrays, lithium batteries and a small diesel generator to power it. Micro-networks need to continue to support clinics, radio relay, weather equipment and safety lighting. Roads may be closed in winter and networks may be unstable for days at a time, so local controllers collect voltage, current, temperature and rescue data every 200 milliseconds and prioritize medical and communications loads when energy is scarce. Complete logging: Only compressed status summaries are sent to the control center when the link is restored. On October 18, 2005, a dust storm caused solar output to drop in fifteen minutes. The temperature of the battery cabinet rose by 34 percent to eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter winds in the morning also showed frequent low-frequency nasal movements. Instead of shutting down the entire power plant, the controller disconnects unnecessary heating devices, reduces partial lighting power and starts the backup generator. Diagnostic modules then suggested three possible causes: solar panels were broken, the surroundings were shaded, windshield bearings wore out, and the contact resistance of the battery connector rose. After the storm weakened, technicians used head-mounted cameras to read the markings, serial numbers and alarm codes of the local processing unit and compare them with the offline maintenance manual. The images are not uploaded to the cloud as they are about critical infrastructure. The capture process first confirms that the entire label is within the safe boundary and checks the clarity of the vertical image and the upper region separately, if the image is cropped, the earpiece is prompted to move left, right or backwards. The target is saved only when the sequence of four syllables is stable and the text is clear enough. The next day's log shows that the automatic sorting is consistent with the artificial judgment of cleaning the panels, replacing the fan bearings, and finally tightening the battery terminals. The disposal took six minutes and critical services were not interrupted. This shows that reliable automation must be interpreted judgementally. EXTRACTED TEXT:
倡远地区混合能源站的自主监测与维护 一座高原试验站依靠太阳能阵列、电池和小型柴油发电机供电。微电 网需要持续支持诊所、无线电中、气象设备和安全照明，冬季道路可能 封闸数日网络也不稳定 因此本地控制器每二百毫秒采集电压、电流、 温度与振动数据，并在能源不足时优先保障医疗和通信负载。完整记录保 存在站内只有压缩后的状态摘要会在链路恢复时发送到控制中心。 二〇二五年十月十八日一场沙尘风暴使太阳能输出在十五分钟内下降 百分之三十四电池柜温度升高八摄氏度，逆变器风扇还出现异常低频摄 动。控制器没有关闭整座电站，而是断开非必要加热装置、降低部分照明 功率井启动各用发电机。诊断模块随后提出三个可能原因：太阳能板被碎 屑遮挡、风扇轴承磨损，以及电池连接器的接触电阻上升。 风暴减弱后，技术员用头戴式摄像设备读取铭牌、序列号和报警代码 本地处理单元再与离线维护手册进行比对。由于资料涉及关键基础设施 图像没有上传云端。采集程序先确认整个标签位干安全边界内并分别检 查全图和上部区域的清晰度，若画面被裁切耳机会提示向左、向右或向 后移动。目标只有连续四帧稳定且文字足够清楚时才会保存。第二天的日 志表明，自动排序与人工判断一致先清理面板，再更换风扇轴承最后 紧固电池端子。处置用了六分钟，关键服务未中断。这说明可靠的自动化 必须解释判断、承认不确定性，并把最终决定留给人。

TRANSLATED TEXT:
Supporting autonomous monitoring and maintenance of far-flung hybrids A highland test station relies on solar arrays, batteries and a small diesel generator to power it. Microwave networks need to continuously support clinics, radios, weather equipment and safety lighting, roads may be blocked for days in winter and networks may not be stable. Therefore, local controllers collect voltage, current, temperature and vibration data every 200 milliseconds, and prioritize medical and communications loads when energy is scarce. Complete logging: Only compressed status summaries are sent to the control center when the link is restored. On October 18, 2005, a dust storm caused solar output to drop in fifteen minutes. The temperature of the battery cabinet rose by 34 percent to eight degrees Celsius, and the inverter fan also showed abnormally low frequency vibrations. The controller does not shut down the entire power plant, but disconnects unnecessary heating devices, lowers partial lighting, power wells, and starts the various generators. The diagnostic module then suggests three possible causes: solar panel breakage, aluminum shielding, fan bearing wear, and increased contact resistance of the battery connector. After the storm weakened, technicians used head-mounted cameras to read the markings, serial numbers and alarm codes of the local processing unit and compare them with the offline maintenance manual. The images are not uploaded to the cloud because of critical infrastructure. The capture process first identifies the entire label within the security boundary and checks separately the clarity of the entire image and the upper area, if the image is cropped, the earpiece is prompted to move left, right or backwards. The target is saved only when the sequence of four syllables is stable and the text is sufficiently clear. The next day's log shows that the automatic sorting is consistent with the artificial judgement of first cleaning the panel, then replacing the fan bearing and finally the tight battery terminal. The disposal took six minutes and critical services were not interrupted. This shows that reliable automation must interpret judgments, acknowledge uncertainty, and leave the final decision to humans.

TRANSLATED TEXT:
Autonomous monitoring and maintenance of hybrid power stations in remote areas A plateau test station relies on solar arrays, lithium batteries and a small diesel generator to power it. Micro-networks need to continue to support clinics, radio relay, weather equipment and safety lighting. Roads may be closed for days in winter, and the network is unstable, so local controllers collect voltage, current, temperature and backup data every 200 milliseconds, and prioritize medical and communications loads when energy is scarce. Complete logs are stored on the station, and only compressed status summaries are sent to the control center when the link is restored. On October 18, 2005, a sandstorm caused the solar output to drop by 34 percent in fifteen minutes, the temperature of the battery cabinet rose by eight degrees Celsius. The inverter fan also showed abnormally low frequency peaks. Instead of shutting down the entire power plant, the controller disconnects unnecessary heating devices, lowers partial lighting, power and starts the backup generator. Diagnostic modules then suggested three possible causes: solar panel breakage, aluminum shielding, fan bearing wear, and increased contact resistance of the battery connector. After the storm weakened, technicians used head-mounted cameras to read the markings, serial numbers and alarm codes of the local processing unit and compare them with the offline maintenance manual. The images are not uploaded to the cloud because of critical infrastructure. The retriever first confirms that the entire label is within the safety boundary and checks the clarity of the entire image and the upper region separately: if the image is cut, the earpiece is prompted to move left, right or backwards. The target is saved only when the sequence of four syllables is stable and the text is sufficiently clear. The next day's logs showed that the automatic sorting was consistent with the artificial judgment: first the panel was cleaned, then the fan bearings were replaced, and finally the battery terminals were tightened. The disposal took six minutes and critical services were not interrupted. This shows that reliable automation must interpret judgments, acknowledge uncertainty, and leave the final decision to humans.
